<div id="review_378631902" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378631902" />
    <a title="Nazia Zennia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4582865-nazia-zennia"><img alt="Nazia Zennia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529774623p2/4582865.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378631902?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nazia Zennia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nazia Zennia" href="/user/show/4582865-nazia-zennia">Nazia Zennia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582865-nazia-zennia?shelf=dystapocalypse">dystapocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582865-nazia-zennia?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582865-nazia-zennia?shelf=hated">hated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582865-nazia-zennia?shelf=total-disapointment">total-disapointment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378631902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6610972531722507480">This 1 star rating was only for one reason and this reason was big enough to eclipse all the good things that was happening in this book. <br/><br/>Let’s start with the good. The world building was great. Descriptions were vivid and although I had no idea how the portals and the multiple planets worked it didn't matter because the story was mostly taking place on earth. The idea was also great and seemed unique with a fresh look in a used setting.<br/><br/>Now for the bad. I didn't like the writing. Although I coul</span>
  <span id="freeText6610972531722507480" style="display:none">This 1 star rating was only for one reason and this reason was big enough to eclipse all the good things that was happening in this book. <br /><br />Let’s start with the good. The world building was great. Descriptions were vivid and although I had no idea how the portals and the multiple planets worked it didn't matter because the story was mostly taking place on earth. The idea was also great and seemed unique with a fresh look in a used setting.<br /><br />Now for the bad. I didn't like the writing. Although I could excuse jargon some of the time (and there were some clever and fitting expressions that were used), it was just too excessive. And the way the story actually played out was so quick and unmemorable that I literally don’t remember what happened in the second half of the book a day later (this could be due to other factors which I will get to shortly). <br /><br />I hated the characters. There wasn’t a single character that I was able to connect to or appreciate or even take the time to understand because I didn’t care about any of them. I fucking hated Jarra. She is one of THE MOST hard core Mary Sues that I have read in the recent past. I couldn’t pay attention to the good points of this book because Jarra was there all the time (the story is in her point of view- fyi) to make me roll my eyes so much I thought they were going to get lodged into the back of my head. <br /><br />Im am so freaking annoyed at how Jarra knew how to do everything ALL THE FUCKING TIME. And hearing her practically brag about it over and over again made me want to flip a desk. Like would you just shut up and learn with every one else? I cant even count the amount of times I had rolled my eyes. I understand the prejudice she has against exos, I understand how she can be bitter about it but regarding skill levels, it seemed like she had no flaws, and she was lucky! Like nothing seemed to go wrong and she didn't seem to be trying at all, making everyone else seem like children. Jarra is good at everything. She knows everything, and is far superior to all the other dolts that are around her. She takes risks that always pay off, she is brave and smart and well-meaning and knows about everything that ever was. BUT she is supposed to be handicapped as she is unable to use Portals to get to other planets. I understand that she is overcompensating. I get it. But to be able to do EVERYTHING is highly, highly improbable, no matter how talented. I would have liked a character that was extremely good at one thing, and that’s how she ended up proving her worth but there was nothing to emphasize why she was being prejudiced, nothing for me to root for her with. I never saw why everyone thought the handicapped were so inferior to all others that they were derogatorily referred to as “apes”. Also, she never gets punished for taking certain risks and endangering the group instead gets rewarded for them because Jarra is perfect. And all her problems get solved quickly and easily. Sigh.<br /><br />I need to stop rolling my eyes. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6610972531722507480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10254940088917029627">I had really high hopes for this book but was simply not impressed. The idea for the book is creative enough but I felt the writing was unbalanced: things that I wish had been pages and pages were only a paragraph, and things that were pages and pages could've been a single sentence. Instead of expanding upon the situations that really could've let the main character's personality shine she truncated them to almost nothing and then spent multiple pages on different types of land-roving vehicles.</span>
  <span id="freeText10254940088917029627" style="display:none">I had really high hopes for this book but was simply not impressed. The idea for the book is creative enough but I felt the writing was unbalanced: things that I wish had been pages and pages were only a paragraph, and things that were pages and pages could've been a single sentence. Instead of expanding upon the situations that really could've let the main character's personality shine she truncated them to almost nothing and then spent multiple pages on different types of land-roving vehicles. Like I said, disappointing, but not to say another wouldn't enjoy it.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=good-heroine">good-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=no-instalove">no-instalove</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552852440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7608602166921997021">First and foremost, I'd like to thank my good friend since my scanlation days, Kureha, for recommending this book to me, because otherwise, I wouldn't have touched this. Not the book's fault, really. Ever since I read (and vehemently disliked) British author Teri Terry's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12743472.Slated__Slated___1_' title='Slated (Slated, #1) by Teri Terry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Slated</a>, I've become wary of English/British YA novels. But thank goodness for angels like my friend, because this novel turned out to be a <i>very</i> pleasant surprise. I loved it! So how do you know if this book is for you? Well, let</span>
  <span id="freeText7608602166921997021" style="display:none">First and foremost, I'd like to thank my good friend since my scanlation days, Kureha, for recommending this book to me, because otherwise, I wouldn't have touched this. Not the book's fault, really. Ever since I read (and vehemently disliked) British author Teri Terry's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12743472.Slated__Slated___1_" title="Slated (Slated, #1) by Teri Terry" rel="nofollow noopener">Slated</a>, I've become wary of English/British YA novels. But thank goodness for angels like my friend, because this novel turned out to be a <i>very</i> pleasant surprise. I loved it! So how do you know if this book is for you? Well, let's run down a checklist for that, shall we?<br /><br /><b>If you like</b><br />* Intellectual heroines with an innate talent for good, snarky comebacks;<br />* slow and steady romances that are nicely developed;<br />* excellently written and well-explained world-building; <br />* slow-paced story telling; and<br />* plots that don't have "OMG, YOU STOLE MY BOYFRIEND! B*ITCH!" or "OMG, HE DOESN'T LOVE ME ENOUGH!" drama, then...<br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK IF FOR YOU!</b><br /> But...<br /><br /><b>If you dislike</b><br />* detailed paragraphs;<br />* pages upon pages of technicalities; <br />* boring love interest; and<br />* too-good-to-be-true, loved-by-everyone, pretty-much-good-at-everything-without-even-trying-heroines, then...<br /><br /><b>You may wanna proceed with caution.</b>:/<br /><br />But despite my list of negative aspects that I found in this book, I'd still recommend it. Perhaps it is because my expectations weren't high to begin with that I deemed myself enjoying it, or mayhap because I considered the snail-like pace refreshing and the lack of intense drama exhilarating, the fact, however, remains that when I finished the book and turned the last page, plastered on my face was a bright and satisfied smile. <br /><br />Granted, Jarra, the main character IS (in a way) a Mary Sue. She's excels in everything she does, and unbelievably so, sometimes; and she's loved and appreciated by everyone. If you know me, then you know I just <b>hate</b> this kind of heroines. <b>BUT!</b> Even though this is so, you'll end up liking her anyway because she's amazingly intellectual, funny, and even snarky. The narration, which is set in a first person POV, just changes everything. So what happened? The Mary-Sue hater in me gave in and rooted for this badass girl to the last page. She does have a flaw, though, and it's her drive to be the best in everything she does (read: highly competitive to the point of... well... irrationality? She does find the error of her ways early, though ;p).<br /><br />For a Dystopian and Science Fiction novel, the world here is extremely well-explained. It's the kind of place I'd love to look forward to someday (without all the apes thing) in the distant future. While I enjoyed the details, the pages upon pages of technicalities in which processes of digging rubble were elaborated made me a bit bored. Of course, they were important and vital to the story, but I felt that it wouldn't have changed anything if there were less of them. Some people may like it, though! Because of this, the story takes on a slow pace. Nothing really big happens. In my opinion, there were no events that would make you go WTF! or FTW!, making it a <i>completely</i> character-driven story. But no worries, the internal narration was fun to read. I'm pretty sure most readers will like Jarra :)<br /><br />All in all, this is a book to look forward to, in my opinion. I loved the world, I loved Jarra and everything about her, including the Mary Sue aspects and all. My love for British writers has been renewed &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="7608602166921997021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1445211599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1445211599" />
    <a title="Penguin_factory" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4411076-penguin-factory"><img alt="Penguin_factory" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327491148p2/4411076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445211599?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penguin_factory" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penguin_factory" href="/user/show/4411076-penguin-factory">Penguin_factory</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4411076-penguin-factory?shelf=dropped">dropped</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445211599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15056295735081241454">I didn't finish this book-- in fact I didn't even get close-- so I can't speak to how well or not it handles its central premise. I will say that I'm immediately leery of a piece of genre fiction that creates a new oppressed class, transposes a lot of the mindset and language (including a name which, if I'm not mistaken, is often seen as derogatory) that applies to a real-life group of people onto them and then spins a story out of it. Is that justified? I don't know, but alarm bells were going </span>
  <span id="freeText15056295735081241454" style="display:none">I didn't finish this book-- in fact I didn't even get close-- so I can't speak to how well or not it handles its central premise. I will say that I'm immediately leery of a piece of genre fiction that creates a new oppressed class, transposes a lot of the mindset and language (including a name which, if I'm not mistaken, is often seen as derogatory) that applies to a real-life group of people onto them and then spins a story out of it. Is that justified? I don't know, but alarm bells were going off during the little I did get through.<br /><br />I stopped reading this book because the writing is atrocious. Characters act like they're high all the time and over-emote wildly, grinning, "grinning crazily", shrieking, jumping up and down, dancing around rooms, throwing shit at each other at the drop of a hat etc. None of this is helped by the fact that the book uses! Lots! of! Exclamation marks!<br /><br />The slang and the awkward future-speak is what really did it for me. In the far future of Earth Girl someone who's interested in history doesn't watch history documentaries; instead they watch history info vids, after which they might kick back with a nice glass of fizzup and scan the ent vid channels for a while. You'd have to be a complete nardle head not to check out the ent vid channels! All your friends will be totally grazzed!<br /><br />Some day I want to understand why "vid" has such a mystical hold on the minds of sci-fi authors. Why do people assume that between now and whenever their book is set we'll abandon all of the words we already use for the technology we've had for over 100 years and use "vid" instead?<br /><br />Maybe this book's plot picks up later, but the bad writing and fingernails-on-chalkboard invented lingo renders that question moot. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15056295735081241454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_772479475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772479475" />
    <a title="Figgy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5056662-figgy"><img alt="Figgy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298984393p2/5056662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/772479475?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Figgy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Figgy" href="/user/show/5056662-figgy">Figgy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5056662-figgy?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5056662-figgy?shelf=rec-khanh-approved">rec-khanh-approved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer772479475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9899088436791181903">I wanted so badly for this to be a five star read. <br/><br/><b>I loved this book.</b> I couldn't put it down, and when I finished reading it last night (up past my bedtime) and went to sleep, I dreamt about this world and the people in it, though more surreal and dream like, of course. My dream back log is often two weeks long, which means something that happens in the real world won't show up in Dreamland for about fourteen days. This jumped the subconscious queue. <br/><br/><br/><b>There were a couple of consistency and other </b></span>
  <span id="freeText9899088436791181903" style="display:none">I wanted so badly for this to be a five star read. <br /><br /><b>I loved this book.</b> I couldn't put it down, and when I finished reading it last night (up past my bedtime) and went to sleep, I dreamt about this world and the people in it, though more surreal and dream like, of course. My dream back log is often two weeks long, which means something that happens in the real world won't show up in Dreamland for about fourteen days. This jumped the subconscious queue. <br /><br /><br /><b>There were a couple of consistency and other errors</b>, such as Fian remarking towards the end of the book that he had never seen snow before, when their first day in the impact suits they looked out on a New York which was now covered in snow, which was not how Jarra had seen it on past trips there. <br /><br /><b>The language could have been explained better.</b> I still don't know what "grazzed" is supposed to mean, though I'm pretty sure it was used with both good and bad vibes. Is it supposed to be shock?<br />Also, "powered" seems to mean any of the following: excited, happy, dunk, drugged, stoned, horny. <br /><br />I really did like how they had their own developments in their language, as it should be after 700 years, but I was a bit confused as to their definite meaning. If they have one. <br /><br /><br /><b>The concept is really interesting, the writing style shows skill and talent, I loved the voice, the characters are fleshed out, the world building is fantastic, and I totally wanted to be Jarra's best friend. <br /><br />I adored Jarra,</b> and loved the little boost of confidence that JMK gave to the Jarra who was somehow totally out of her element, yet so very in it at the same time. I didn't love<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[JMK. When Jarra had a mental break, and JMK came out to drive for a while and protect Jarra, I didn't love who JMK was. She was far too cocky.<br /><br />She just wasn't Jarra.<br /><br />Now, really, before you go objecting, I understand that this was well written by the author, for me to long for Jarra's return because I didn't like JMK, the persona Jarra had created. But after a while of JMK being in the driver's seat, being cocky and obnoxious, I got really BORED.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />Don't get me wrong. <b>At no point during this book did I find myself wishing it was over</b>, or wishing I could just put it down and walk away from it. I <b>HAD</b> to read it, I <b>HAD</b> to know how it would all work out for Jarra and the rest of the class. <br /><br /><br />I really, really enjoyed it. <br /><br /><br /><b>But I feel like I was robbed.</b> <br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was a scene I was waiting for all book. <br /><br />Call me sadistic, call me a Schadenfreude seeker, call me pretty much anything you want. They might be true, but I don't think they're the reason for this particular feeling. <br /><br />I spent <b>ALL BOOK</b> waiting for that moment when the class would find out, or Jarra would tell them, that she was handicapped. I wanted to see their <b>reactions</b>. I wanted to see how <b>Krath</b> would react when he found out the person he had been hitting on was an "ape".<br /><br />Instead, Jarra is in an induced coma for a week due to injuries that need time to heal, and she wakes up to be told by Fian that he broke the news to the class. <br /><br />Yes, I realise that is likely a thing he would do, especially if he was worried that Jarra was going to back out and run away instead. But YOU ROBBED ME, FIAN! And that goes for you too, Janet Edwards. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />I WILL be reading the next book. In fact, I ordered it when I ordered the first and am still waiting for it to show up. <br /><br /><b>I was devastated when I got home to an empty mailbox and the knowledge that there is no post tomorrow because it's New Year's Day.</b> <br /><br />I'll see you and your Earth Star in 2014 Ms. Edwards. (Didn't mean that to sound quite so naughty or sinister.)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9899088436791181903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781616147655" href="/book/show/16246712-earth-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=kapk">kapk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=play-book-tag">play-book-tag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=book-1">book-1</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=british-author">british-author</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048682-karin?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2079167553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7840587351725333714">4.5 stars <br/><br/>So, an update now that I have just read it a second time--I still think this is worth 4.5 stars. The writing is good, the characters are well developed, the pacing is excellent, the future world building solid and consistent and the story full of adventure, action, a bit of romance, character growth and dealing with differences between people. The review I wrote in 2017 includes a bit about what the story is actually about. Why someone else originally shelved this as extraterrestrials </span>
  <span id="freeText7840587351725333714" style="display:none">4.5 stars <br /><br />So, an update now that I have just read it a second time--I still think this is worth 4.5 stars. The writing is good, the characters are well developed, the pacing is excellent, the future world building solid and consistent and the story full of adventure, action, a bit of romance, character growth and dealing with differences between people. The review I wrote in 2017 includes a bit about what the story is actually about. Why someone else originally shelved this as extraterrestrials is a bit of a mystery to me, but I am guessing it is because of the exos--humans who live on other planets and look down on the Handicapped, aka apes.<br /><br />Jarra was sent to earth for life immediately after birth because of her Handicap. She will die from anaphylactic shock if she goes to any other planet. Undaunted, she applies for an off-world university that studies pre-History on earth and makes up a fictional background so that the other students think she is normal, and not an ape. But once on the dig site in ancient New York she finds that the exos are a lot different than she expected. My summary is lame compared with the book.<br /><br />Sure, the title is rather lame and this is young adult, but it was better than I expected. At the start I was thinking it was okay, but it deserved to win the Bookworm Award for Best Fiction and probably more than that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7840587351725333714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_767842171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/767842171" />
    <a title="Nafiza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza"><img alt="Nafiza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529831446p2/2483439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/767842171?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafiza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafiza" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza">Nafiza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=source-library">source-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer767842171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3793742097056814848">This novel has a fantastic premise. A girl who is trapped on earth while the rest of humanity travels through the universe, living on newly discovered planets and just being cooler. Then she decides to go to a foreign (as in a different planet) university that holds its mandatory history course (program?) on earth (which makes sense since they’re studying human history). Apparently, in the future, archaeology is a pretty darn big deal because earth is reverting to natural status and human beings</span>
  <span id="freeText3793742097056814848" style="display:none">This novel has a fantastic premise. A girl who is trapped on earth while the rest of humanity travels through the universe, living on newly discovered planets and just being cooler. Then she decides to go to a foreign (as in a different planet) university that holds its mandatory history course (program?) on earth (which makes sense since they’re studying human history). Apparently, in the future, archaeology is a pretty darn big deal because earth is reverting to natural status and human beings no longer know how to deal with feral things like wolves (other than scream and run, you’d think they’d have them under control by now) – anyway, I’m rambling.<br /><br />So yeah, Jarra, aka the Earth Girl, goes to the foreign university that is doing an extended field trip on earth and starts lying. She lies profusely about who she is, where she comes from, who her parents are. Everything. But she is pretty superawesomessauce special snowflake so she knows more than the instructor and in fact, she lectures the class (which means a whole lot of telling in the narrative, like A LOT) and then she is better than everyone at everything. She saves people, she has boys wanting her, the military gives her some kind of honor because IT IS A COINCIDENCE but all those lies she told about her military background? They’re ALL true.<br /><br />It started to get ridiculous around the time her parents die one page after she finds them again. Whoops, spoiler. What happens after that is even more ridiculous.<br /><br />Jarra is a Mary Sue.<br /><br />She is the Mary Sue-ist Sue there ever was and she probably throws up rainbows. She can’t do anything wrong. The world is created well and were it peopled with characters more interesting, engaging and flawed than Jarra, I dare say I would have enjoyed the novel a whole lot. However, the fact that Jarra can do no wrong is a major deterrent where enjoyment is concerned. Everyone loves her, forgives her for lying and accepts her because she’s too wonderful not to accept. The military gives her the highest honor there is for a reason I’m still unclear on. Her boyfriend’s parents accept her even though we are told the mother does not like Earthbound people at all. Her boyfriend gets over his anger at being deceived very quickly. Her friends shrug it away and just.<br /><br />I did not like the book. There are parts of it that I found interesting but I found it difficult to believe that people would be so irresponsible to let the infrastructure of major cities simply fall to ruin. Were New York city to be vacated due to a major migration to space, you can bet your pants that people would at the very least dispose of flammable chemicals etc. The only way I would accept that people simply left things as they were (open can of coffee on the counter) is if they evacuated in a hurry. It is human nature to pack up and put away in case of absences. So yeah, I had trouble with the logistics of the novel, the characters and the basic plot. I don’t think I’d recommend it but you may have a different reaction to Jarra than I did. (I can’t even think about her without rolling my eyes.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3793742097056814848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_696109774" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696109774" />
    <a title="Maree" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5001811-maree"><img alt="Maree" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304369647p2/5001811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696109774?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maree" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maree" href="/user/show/5001811-maree">Maree</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5001811-maree?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696109774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer23512602448493613">I was absolutely enthralled with Jarra and her story. Now that Earth has portalling tech to instantly travel from world to world, they've explored and settled on many. But there are still those babies that are born and can't survive on worlds other than Earth. They have to be sent back immediately, and anyone who has one automatically assumes their partner has old ancient genes. These children are raised by the hospitals on Earth with every benefit, but they can never leave the planet. Everyone </span>
  <span id="freeText23512602448493613" style="display:none">I was absolutely enthralled with Jarra and her story. Now that Earth has portalling tech to instantly travel from world to world, they've explored and settled on many. But there are still those babies that are born and can't survive on worlds other than Earth. They have to be sent back immediately, and anyone who has one automatically assumes their partner has old ancient genes. These children are raised by the hospitals on Earth with every benefit, but they can never leave the planet. Everyone assumes they're apes, unintelligent, unable to perform like normal humans. And predictably, Jarra wants to prove them wrong.<br /><br />Jarra is totally bull headed, and loves history. So she decides to do something different--apply for a university offworld in pre-history, the first year of which has to be done on Earth doing excavations. And no one in her class will be the wiser!<br /><br />I really loved how Jarra thought. She assumed it would be great to laugh at the exos once she had earned their respect and found out she was only an ape. But as she got to know them, her feelings changed. She's a complicated mess, an orphan abandoned by her parents and desperate to prove herself. I was totally taken with her and how she commanded her classmates from the start. Her self-created identity was creative and RESEARCHED! So she didn't get herself into to trouble by slipping up in the normal way.<br /><br />But her psychosis when she receives some terrible news and actually thinks she is Jarra, Military child was a bit weird. I'm not sure I totally believe it, but at that point I was more than willing to go along.<br /><br />The really fascinating part about having a character going to university for history is that it isn't at all odd to be hearing lectures about the world after our current time and how it transformed. I feel like I know a ton about the world, which is rich in history and details. That's something not a lot of scifi tends to have these days. A lot of it is pretty simplistic. I also loved reading about the futuristic excavation of New York City with all the technology they use. I actually feel like I could see a dig site and know what was going on! Great detail. It kind of reminded me of the Pern books in that way, which is something I indefinitely love.<br /><br />Need the next book now! I was a little surprised with how they left things and how the big reveal was kind of played down. It's definitely a complete ending, but not what you'd expect at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="23512602448493613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_309916294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309916294?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Angel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Angel" href="/user/show/4731969-andy-angel">Andy Angel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309916294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2416554797814274179"> First things first, this review is from an uncorrected proof copy - the book will be available to buy in the shops on August 16th.<br/> The year is 2788 and thanks to the use of portals mankind has now moved out to the stars. <br/> Unfortunately, due to a problem with the immune system, a small percentage of humans are only able to survive on Earth. Portalling off planet would mean death unless they can be sent straight back to Earth and hospitalised. These people, know as "handicapped or apes" (amongst </span>
  <span id="freeText2416554797814274179" style="display:none"> First things first, this review is from an uncorrected proof copy - the book will be available to buy in the shops on August 16th.<br /> The year is 2788 and thanks to the use of portals mankind has now moved out to the stars. <br /> Unfortunately, due to a problem with the immune system, a small percentage of humans are only able to survive on Earth. Portalling off planet would mean death unless they can be sent straight back to Earth and hospitalised. These people, know as "handicapped or apes" (amongst other things) are seen as an underclass.<br /> Our heroine in this book, Jarra, is one of these "apes" but she is determined to prove she is eqqual to, if not better than, the off-worlders (or "exo"s). To this end, she enrolls on a Pre-History Foundation Course with University Asgard which is based at dig sites around Planet Earth. By not having to leave Earth for the course Jarra believes she can hide her handicap and pass off as normal to her classmates.<br /> Jarra invents a backstory for herself as Jarra Military Kid (JMK) but is often nearly caught out, until she gets some shock news and actually starts to believe her JMK persona and life is real.<br />This is a really well thought out story, with believable science that doesn't require you to have a phd in astrophysics. The idea of the old cities of Earth being abandoned as people headed for the stars makes sense. We only get to see the New York site but that is so well described and atmospheric that, especially when the team move from the fringe site to New York Main, the city/ ruins almost becomes a character itself.<br /> Each off system has its' own character traits which makes for an interesting student group and maybe Jarra is not the only one with a secret!<br />This book will appeal to people who like things like the Hunger Games series but also to a wider audience and, in my opinion, it has massive potential for being made into a movie (I really want to see New York Main and the solar storm on the big screen).<br /> Another, final, plus for me - the book ties up neatly at the end. There may be more from Jarra, Earth Girl, but if there isn't, there are no real loose threads left dangling.<br />A 5* book from a promising new author <br /><br />Post a Comment<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2416554797814274179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13070298362002726733">This book was a fun and imaginative story about a teen girl in the future of Earth. I became interested in it because of the theme of a handicapped girl dealing with the stigma of her situation and trying to overcome it. The story does address the issue in a sensitive way that both adults and teens will understand. The world created in the story and the characters seem to jump off the page. The pace is fast most of the time which is something I enjoyed. However, there were some parts which seeme</span>
  <span id="freeText13070298362002726733" style="display:none">This book was a fun and imaginative story about a teen girl in the future of Earth. I became interested in it because of the theme of a handicapped girl dealing with the stigma of her situation and trying to overcome it. The story does address the issue in a sensitive way that both adults and teens will understand. The world created in the story and the characters seem to jump off the page. The pace is fast most of the time which is something I enjoyed. However, there were some parts which seemed to drag a bit for me. The ending was built up by the author and I anticipated it with a lot of suspense throughout. I have to say, the ending was a let down for me though. I will have to think about why it happened the way it did.</span>

<div id="review_645435435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645435435" />
    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645435435?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil (or bleed)" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed">Neil (or bleed)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645435435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2471985048524122684">This book caught my interest without seeking my permission. The whole concept of the book, for me, is ingenious and engrossing. <br/><br/>The setting is, of course, futuristic, post-apocalyptic; being Earth as not the only planet that mankind can live. Yes, many planets, became the habitats of the people. And Earth was just a home for the Handicapped, an ape. This kind of setting intrigued me.<br/><br/>Character development for the MC is zan! Totally zan! Jarra, the MC, wants to prove herself to the 'exos' that she</span>
  <span id="freeText2471985048524122684" style="display:none">This book caught my interest without seeking my permission. The whole concept of the book, for me, is ingenious and engrossing. <br /><br />The setting is, of course, futuristic, post-apocalyptic; being Earth as not the only planet that mankind can live. Yes, many planets, became the habitats of the people. And Earth was just a home for the Handicapped, an ape. This kind of setting intrigued me.<br /><br />Character development for the MC is zan! Totally zan! Jarra, the MC, wants to prove herself to the 'exos' that she is not just your ordinary girl/ape. And it is amazing how the author build her character until she gets what she wants. I loved her really. Her wit, sarcasm, charm, all that. I can't stop loving her. Besides, I also enjoyed some characters especially the Team 1 where Jarra belongs. They have different amusing talents and personalities given that they came from different planet sector. <br /><br />The plot of the story isn't confusing. I go with the flow. The pacing is good. I wasn't left hanging. And my imagination to picture this worked well. Although, the book revolved, somehow, with the digging and tagging or should I say, learning History. Since I'm into history, no doubt I enjoyed it. My feels are in them when they do the digging-tagging scenario; discovering something, you know.<br /><br />The only problem, in my opinion, is that I didn't see any major conflict for the MC. I don't know, maybe, I can't consider what I've read conflict as a major conflict though it still gave me tension. <br /><br />What I really admire with this one is the technology, superiorly, the communications technology. From portals, to lookups, to gadgets and all that. WOW! How advance. How I wish I can experience using that.<br /><br />Indeed, I really enjoyed this page turner, attention catcher book. Totally AMAZ!! I'm rooting to read the second one, to know what adventure will Jarra is facing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2471985048524122684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_841842188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/841842188" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/841842188?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer841842188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6277897600690276634">There are twists in a book, and then there are twists! This book had such a crazy twist in the middle of it, and I loved it!<br/><br/>Jarra, the main character, is stuck on Earth while most people are able to travel to other planets, because she is "handicapped," like 1 in every 1,000 people. Her people are looked down upon and she has some major anger issues. Her whole goal, in the beginning of the book, is to get revenge on all of those whom have looked down upon her by enrolling in a college that is at</span>
  <span id="freeText6277897600690276634" style="display:none">There are twists in a book, and then there are twists! This book had such a crazy twist in the middle of it, and I loved it!<br /><br />Jarra, the main character, is stuck on Earth while most people are able to travel to other planets, because she is "handicapped," like 1 in every 1,000 people. Her people are looked down upon and she has some major anger issues. Her whole goal, in the beginning of the book, is to get revenge on all of those whom have looked down upon her by enrolling in a college that is attended by those who can travel, rather than one with other "handicapped" people like herself. But, after getting to know them, she realizes that she had also been prejudiced and things get crazy - I mean, literally crazy.<br /><br />The characters in the book are pretty good, and varied. The thing that I didn't really like about Jarra, at first, was her arrogance and the fact that she was too good at absolutely everything. It was annoying! But, it was interesting to see how all of the characters developed from shallow, what you might expect, to deeper people with problems like everyone else. The world building was fun, but I would have enjoyed hearing more about the other planets and hope that we do in the future books. One of the best things about the book was how easily it flowed and the interaction between the characters. The worst part, for me, was when the descriptions of the excavations went on and on a bit too long. I would rather have had those pages devoted to more interactions between the characters instead of her listing which beams or pieces of concrete she decided needed to be moved. Despite that, it was a very fun book to read and I am looking forward to the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6277897600690276634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2409137714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2409137714" />
    <a title="Elisabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7099433-elisabeth"><img alt="Elisabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330542568p2/7099433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2409137714?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elisabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elisabeth" href="/user/show/7099433-elisabeth">Elisabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781616147655" href="/book/show/16246712-earth-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7099433-elisabeth?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7099433-elisabeth?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2409137714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14916303591710682850">Looks dumb, is great fun.<br/><br/>One of the jacket reviews calls it "utopian YA" and indeed it's a refreshing shift from the usual misery: conflict and drama ARE possible without everything being horrible all the time! The character voice of course makes a huge difference, and Jarra's is a delight; the world-creation is brilliantly dense and well-thought-out; the infodumps are delivered believably in-story. Even the invented language feels completely natural. It hits all the YA sci fi tropes - hyper-com</span>
  <span id="freeText14916303591710682850" style="display:none">Looks dumb, is great fun.<br /><br />One of the jacket reviews calls it "utopian YA" and indeed it's a refreshing shift from the usual misery: conflict and drama ARE possible without everything being horrible all the time! The character voice of course makes a huge difference, and Jarra's is a delight; the world-creation is brilliantly dense and well-thought-out; the infodumps are delivered believably in-story. Even the invented language feels completely natural. It hits all the YA sci fi tropes - hyper-competent teenage protag, boarding school, post-apocalypse (everyone's left Earth), star-crossed romance - without once hitting a puerile note. Many props to author Edwards for both concept and execution.<br /><br />It reminds me of Lois Bujold's Barrayar series, in which hero Miles falls relentlessly into scrape after improbable scrape and still finds a way to shine - and the audience can't help but enjoy the ride. <br /><br />Recommended for those who want some fun for a change, with no sacrifice of storytelling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14916303591710682850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571752021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15416760631732899262">I tried hard to get into this book, I really did, but I just couldn’t do it. This wasn’t bad, it was just boring. The pacing was incredibly slow, and I made it 145 pages in without there being a clear plot. Yes, the book is about Jarra pretending to be a “norm” instead of a handicapped earth girl, but once we reach the setting of the pretense, the only thing leading the reader on was when the others would find out, and that is not enough to create an interesting narrative. I couldn’t see what wo</span>
  <span id="freeText15416760631732899262" style="display:none">I tried hard to get into this book, I really did, but I just couldn’t do it. This wasn’t bad, it was just boring. The pacing was incredibly slow, and I made it 145 pages in without there being a clear plot. Yes, the book is about Jarra pretending to be a “norm” instead of a handicapped earth girl, but once we reach the setting of the pretense, the only thing leading the reader on was when the others would find out, and that is not enough to create an interesting narrative. I couldn’t see what would happen in the rest of the book, besides Jarra being amazing at Earth digs. I think the concept was interesting, and the world built here was amazing, but there wasn’t enough anywhere else to keep me reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15416760631732899262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tS/5XXjKn+d1AkOYhLhgmgteqx2CuGHscd5QqD+6BYquwp1GRjUE5YDxDW7YbdyCGk6spWyXEeLZi1t8oF3JCg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UHxICLZKeT6MqNBar1WtLZe0ogiR8JHGrj8vGcWxNLBLkSwTiLXiPHlbnqzzgBE1hqSlsH/f4cgGaiTNWlb4MA==')})
  }

Wh<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14890747266746483762\" style=\"display:none\">She works at a space station catering to everyone else’s virtual fantasies. When a man gets stuck in the scenario she must wake the sleeping prince.\n\n\nStyra works at the Blue Station and has been programming since she was able to reach a keyboard. When she became and adult she went from writing the simple scenarios and backgrounds to guiding tangled clients through the environments they had selected. Lately, she has been going in to pry out the difficult cases and making sure that everyone plays by the rules. Her boss calls her in on her day off and sends her in after an imperial captain.
